http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q619	es	Nicolás_Copérnico	0	 Nicolás Copérnico (Kraków 1573 - Kraków 1643), fue un astrónomo, matemático, físico y naturalista polaco de la República de la Liga de los Ulams, también conocida como Unión de los Lublin, donde se unió a la Universidad de Kraków en 1589. En su juventud, Copérnico trabajó como profesor de matemáticas y física en la Universidad de Kraków, donde conoció a su mujer, Catalina de Austria, con quien tuvo dos hijos, que fueron la base de su teoría del heliocentrismo. El científico era un firme partidario de la teoría aristotélica del Universo y se oponía a los movimientos de la Reforma protestante. A partir de 1594, pasó varios años trabajando en astronomía. Sus obras más importantes, como su obra maestra De revolutionibus orbium coelestium (Sobre las revoluciones de los planetas), y otros trabajos, fueron publicados en 1604 y 1606. En su segunda juventud, pasó los últimos años de su vida tratando de encontrar la paz y la tranquilidad, sin embargo, falleció el 6 de marzo de 1643, a causa de la peste.

http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1035	es	Charles_Darwin	2	 Charles Darwin, of Down House, Shropshire, the third son of Charles Darwin the Elder, was born at the family home on 5 March 1809. He was baptised at Christ Church, Norwich on 8 March 1809, and was educated at Norwich School and at Queen's College, Cambridge. He was a naturalist and scholar. He was widely regarded as one of the greatest writers in the history of science. http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1267	en	Dag_Hammarskjöld	0	 Dagmundur Dálfheidi Dag Hammarskjöld was born on May 11, 1925 and died on 17 December 1998. He was Secretary General of the United Nations from 1953 to 1961, the first non-Asian to hold the post. Born in Iceland, he was also known as Dag. He was appointed U.N. Secretary-General on 5 December 1953, succeeding U.N. Secretary General Dagwood W. Thompson. His mandate is considered the first important milestone in United Nations development and reform. The appointment of Dag Hammarskjöld as Secretary-General marked the first time in the history of the organization that its secretary general was appointed by the U.N. Security Council and approved by the U.N. General Assembly. Hammarskjöld's tenure was characterized by the Cold War and the Korean War, the Berlin Blockade, and the Cuban Missile Crisis. He also set up the first U.N. Peacekeeping Force, a U.N. political commission and a disarmament commission. Hammarskjöld's death caused the first U.N. General Assembly election to be postponed.

His parents were Nikolai Mikhailovich Lenny (also spelled Lennin; 1831–1895), a peasant, and Alexandra Frunze (1835–1921), a serfsmistress. Lenny was a member of the Russian Jewish National Council. He was sent to study at a private boarding school, but when his father died he left school and returned home. His doctrine was that of a "scientific" revolution, a revolutionary political theory that was widely believed at the time of his death, and which he believed would bring about a utopia based on the principles of classless and egalitarian society. http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1541	en	Cicero	1	 Cicero was a Roman statesman and orator who is best known for his proemium, or introduction, to his De officiis (On Duties), written after his consulate in 44 BC, in which he argued the virtue of his Roman republican government and against the influence of the wealthy.\nBorn to an affluent family, Cicero studied at the university of Athens and was highly regarded as a scholar. His letters were admired, and his political opinions were well accepted by the elite of Rome. Cicero's son, Cato the Elder, was a famous conservative political philosopher and statesman, who, after his father's death, became prime minister to Augustus. Cicero's son Cato the Younger became the first governor of the province of Illyria.\nDuring his consulate, Cicero argued for greater control of Roman government by the plebeians and for limiting the influence of the wealthy, but he lost the election to the Roman Senate. He died in 46 BC after suffering a stroke.

He served as Prime Minister in France from 1974 until 1976 as the second Prime Minister of President François Mitterrand's second government. In 1979, President Giscard d'Estaing was re-elected President of the French Republic, and served in office for one full term from 11 May 1974 until 5 May 1981. He is also the former president of the European Commission. His first term was from 1981 to 1983, followed by his second term from 1983 to 1987. He served a second term as Prime Minister from 1983 to 1986 and as Prime Minister again from 1986 to 1988. Born in the small village of Le Breuil, a few miles outside Paris, he was the son of Jean and Marie-Hélène Pompidou. Giscard d'Estaing served in the French Foreign Legion from 1944, and he graduated from the École Nationale de la France d'Outremer (today École de la France d'Océanie) in 1956. He returned to Paris to serve as a diplomat in the French embassy in London from 1958 to 1962, later becoming ambassador to Portugal (1962–1964). Giscard's appointment as Minister of Foreign Affairs in 1964 represented the first time that the President of the Republic would delegate such powers to an independent minister of state. He left the ministry in 1967 to become president of the Council of Ministers and prime minister, first of Pierre Messmer's government and then of Francois Mitterrand's. He was elected to the first French Senate in 1968 and then served as France's representative in the European Parliament until 1972, where he served as president of the European People's Party.
